45 EQTC:Quests:Luclin:Rallic Pack Rallic Pack <p>
<i>This quest produces a 10-slot, 85% weight reduction, container that can hold giant-sized items. </i>
</p> 
<p>
Speak with Rallik in the city of Katta Castellum; he's located in the building resembling a church, with a hedge around it, right next to the Tenebrous zone (loc -101, -39). Enter the building, take the left hall to the end, turn left, he'll be the door on the left. He was indifferent to be as a Tribunal-worshipping shaman, but KOS to a Cazic Thule monk. Hail him, follow the dialog, he asks you to bring back information from a courier. 
</p> 
<p>
The mob you want is called 'a grimling runner'. It can be found in the Tenebrous Mtns; it spawns on the south side of the zone, right along the wall. If you're coming from the Grimling Forest, turn left after you zone and hug the wall. For me, it spawned on the hill just before the first grimling mine, and pathed toward the mine. It drops a bag, the bag is LORE and NODROP, and not really a bag (it will fit in your bags, just make sure you have a medium sized slot available). Give the bag to Rallik, he will give you the (lore) rallic pack pattern. 
</p> 
<p>
Next you will need a perfect owlbear pelt. Many owlbears can be found in Hollowshade Moor at the owlbear caves. The loc is approximately 2000, 1000. 
</p> 
<p>
Finally you'll need to head to the newbie area of Shadeweaver's Thicket, just outside of Shar Vahl, or the newbie pit in Shar Vahl. You want shadeling silks, which you can get from xakra silkworms, or the lesser shades that roam in the northern part of Shadeweavers. You'll need 8 silks total to make 1 shade silk cord and 1 shade silk thread (2 silks = thread, 3 threads = cord). Combine cord, thread, pelt and pattern into a sewing kit (a coldain tanning kit also works) and you create a Rallic pack. Trivial is <=15
</p> 1066 2003-05-28 09:11:59 2003-05-28 09:11:59 EQTC Editor Krazick 0 0 2003-05-28 09:11:48 EQTC Editor Krazick
139 EQTC:Quests:Luclin:Seru Bane Seru Bane Weapons <p>
Weapons with the Seru Bane attribute are needed to be able to damage Lord Inquisitor Seru through normal melee. Procs on non bane weapons will land on him, but to keep up a continuous run of ?normal? melee damage, you need a Seru weapon with Bane DMG: Seru +# to be able to hit him. 
</p> 
<p>
Lord Inquisitor Seru is located in Sanctus Seru, and all of the items needed to make Seru Bane weapons are located in various zones of the SoL expansion. You will be traveling around and camping various things to make these weapons, so do not expect it to be as simple as making things such as normal forged weapons. 
</p> 
<p>
<strong>The original text for making the Seru Bane weapons: </strong>
</p> 
<p>
Book 1: <br />
 <u>Day 1</u><br />
 Today is a great day, so I shall begin this journal. The High Inquisitor has called for my skilled hand to create for him a set of armor, which cannot be pierced by any weapon. This is to be my last chance to be in good grace with Lord Seru, though I have denounced Katta I assume they can still sense that I miss my family. Regardless, I shall begin working with the materials that were supplied to me in the morning. 
</p> 
<p>
<u>Day 2</u><br />
 Creation is going steady; the ore is melting to my expectations. This metal, which I have named Yttrium, should not be able to be pierced. I have sent for items to help tint the armor as Lord Seru requests. 
</p> 
<p>
<u>Day 10</u><br />
 With the greaves complete I begin working on the Breastplate soon. I have discovered how to make perfect Yttrium Sheets so production should go faster. Mixing two bricks of Yttruim ore, with one Vial of Quicksilver Temper creates the perfect sheet. The Quicksilver Temper is a harder mixture though, I must request ingredients be brought to me often, they seem to be hard to come by. For the perfect hue I have been brewing one part Fungoid Sap, one part Meteor Dust, one part Shissar Blood, and one part Shiknar Ichor. I do not know where the Consillium of the Hand is acquiring these ingredients, nor do I care, as long as I can present Lord Seru with a fine set of armor. 
</p> 
<p>
<u>Day 18</u><br />
 I have finished Lord Seru's Breastplate and just returned from presenting the Praesertum with it. They shall take it to him soon, so I should get word in a week. I shall wait to see if this is enough to please Lord Seru. I shall begin work on weapons that can match the armor, in the case that it doesn't. 
</p> 
<p>
<br />
 Book 2: <br />
<u>Day 22</u><br />
 Success! I have created an entire arsenal that should be able to strike through his armor. I had the most success using the following: A Pommel Mold, Hilt Mold, one Vial of Quicksilver Temper, one Yttrium Steel Sheet, and either a Dagger, Short, Curved, or Long Blade mold created a fine blade. An Oak Shaft, one Vial of Quicksilver Temper, one Yttrium Steel Sheet, and either a Mace, Hammer, or Axe Head Mold created heavier, powerful weapons. For a powerful set of gloves, I used two High Quality Rockhopper Pelts, one Vial of Quicksilver Temper, and one Yttrium Steel Sheet. A bow made with an Oak Bow Staff, a Silk String, a Planing Tool, one Yttrium Sheet Metal, and one Vial of Quicksilver Temper imbues any arrow shot from it with the same properties. Should I be banished, I will create these weapons for Recuso to destroy Seru. 
</p> 
<p>
<u>Day 25</u><br />
 The inevitable has happened. My time for the question has arisen, even though too soon. I failed because of my longing for my family Katta. I know their ways are wrong but I of course still love them. I write into this log from a land of destitution, I have been named a Recuso. 
</p> 
<p>
<u>Day 49</u><br />
 A few days ago in search of shelter from the rain I stumbled inside this place. What is this place... my nightmares become reality. I feel as though I am being watched with every step. I can not remember the way out, I can not remember... anything. 
</p> 
<p>
Quicksilver Temper is brewed and trivial below 180. The Yttrium Steel Sheet has a high trivial somewhere above 250. Both of these items are droppable. The final combines' trivial levels are in the mid to upper 100s. The final weapons are no drop, so you have to produce them yourself. 
</p> 
<p>
<strong>Combines in brief: </strong><br />
 A VIAL OF QUICKSILVER TEMPER: shissar blood + shiknar ichor + fungoid sap + meteor dust <br />
 YTTRIUM SHEET METAL: 2 small bricks of yttrium ore + quicksilver temper 
</p> 
<ul> 
<li>Shissar blood can be found on the snake-type shissar mobs in Luclin, mainly in Ssra. temple, and also available in the grey. </li> 
<li> Fungoid sap is only dropped off An Ancient Shrieker, which resides in the Deep. There are a couple of camps of them on the far side of the invisible bridge. They are KoS and assist each other. Drop rate is said to be uncommon-rare. </li> 
<li> Meteor dust is found mainly in the Grey, from Shattered golems, shissar style mobs, and rarely from the skeleton version of the sun revenants. </li> 
<li> Shiknar ichor is found on the Shik'nar bug type mobs in Fungus grove. Any form of Shik'nar insect can drop it. 
</ul> <hr> 
<p>
 
</p><b>Trivials for the below are reported as <=127</b><p>

46 EQTC:Quests:Luclin:SHTrading Shadow Haven - Register for Trading <p>
<i>While this quest is not really a tradeskill quest, it is an important one for tradesfolk who wish to operate out of the Shadow Haven area. The quest results in an Amulet of the Haven (magic, lore, no drop): AC 1, CHA 2. It also adjusts several factions in the area, making it easier to shop there. Some merchants will still be dubious after completing the quest, so you may need to loop it several times (or do other quests) before you can shop with all the merchants.</i>
</p> 
<p>
It starts in Shadow Haven with Trade Commissioner Henry, after you hail him ...
</p> 
<p>
Trade Commissioner Henry says 'Hello there, traveler. I don't believe that I have seen you around these parts before- then again, I could have and simply forgotten since there have been so many new faces around here. However, if you are a newcomer to Shadowhaven, please make sure that you [register for trading] in the Haven. Registering with the Traders of the Haven will legitimize you in the eyes of local merchants and customers. 
</p> 
<p>
You say, 'register for trading'
</p> 
<p>
Trade Commissioner Henry says 'It's great that you are interested _____, you will surely be glad you did. I have some simple deliveries that I need completed if you wish to be a registered trader in Shadowhaven. 
</p> 
<p>
You say, 'what deliveries?'
</p> 
<p>
Trade Commissioner Henry says 'The deliveries are simple enough, I just need you to bring some letters to some merchants of the Haven that are currently working in other locations. Will you [deliver these letters]? 
</p> 
<p>
You say, 'I will deliver these letters'
</p> 
<p>
Trade Commissioner Henry says 'I surely do appreciate the help, _____- clearly you understand the value of solid relations with the locals. First, I will need you to take this newsletter to Sateal. He is currently on assignment in the Bazaar and has been out of the loop on the happenings of Shadowhaven because of his heavy workload. Bring this to him and then return to me with his sales report. I look forward to seeing you soon. 
</p> 
<p>
Receive a newsletter and bring it to Sateal in The Bazaar (inside the large merchant area).
</p> 
<p>
Sateal Deirosap says 'Ah great, I have been meaning to go and pick one of these up from the Trade Commissioner but I have been very busy with my work. I'm sure Henry has been waiting for my sales report so here it is. Please return it to him for me if you could and thanks again! 
</p> 
<p>
<i>(You receive only experience for this portion of the quest.)</i>
</p> 
<p>
Receive sales report and bring it back to Trade Commissioner Henry.
</p> 
<p>
Trade Commissioner Henry says 'Great to see you back so soon _____, you looked like a dependable person from the start. The next thing I need you to do is a bit more dangerous, but by the looks of you I doubt it will be a problem. Go to the Shadowhaven outpost in Fungusgrove and give Thar this book. Thar is a great merchant but I have seen his sales steadily declining, so I figured this book full of selling tips will help him regain his confidence and help him produce the kinds of numbers I know he is capable of. If his economy report is ready please, bring that back to me when you return. 
</p> 
<p>
<i>(You receive only experience for this portion of the quest.)</i>
</p> 
<p>
Receive book of selling tips and take to Thar Anton in the merchant area of Fungus Grove.
</p> 
<p>
Thar Anton says 'I see you have brought a book from the Commissioner. Well I'm not much for reading but I will surely try anything that may increase my sales. Anyways I'm sure you arent that interested in how bad my sales are and would like to be on your way so here you go. 
</p> 
<p>
<i>You receive experience and gain faction with Traders of the Haven, House of Fordel, House of Midst and House of Stout</i>
</p> 
<p>
Receive Thar's report and return it to Trade Commissioner Henry.
</p> 
<p>
Trade Commissioner Henry says 'Excellent work _____, I knew that you were someone that I could trust to get the job done. The trader's union of Shadowhaven will hear of your solid work ethic. Perhaps a courier job is in your future, I couldn't have expected anyone to make these deliveries as fast as you did! Please take this amulet as a symbol of your dedication to Shadowhaven's booming economy. While wearing this you are sure to get all the greatest deals from the merchants of the Haven both here and in the bazaar. It was a pleasure meeting, you and thanks for all of your help. 
</p> 
<p>
<i>You receive experience, gain faction with Traders of the Haven, House of Fordel, House of Midst and House of Stout plus receive the Amulet of the Haven. Since the amulet is lore, if you decide to loop this quest, you will receive a duplicate lore message when you hand in Thar's report, but you will still receive the faction adjustments. </i>

47 EQTC:Quests:Luclin:SonicWolfBane Shar Vahl - Sonic Wolf Bane Weapons <p>
<i>This quest requires the cooperation of all five Vah Shir classes, and requires that they have first completed their class-specific quests. It results in the creation of a weapon, and then sends you back to your guild for further questing.</i>
</p> 
<p>
<i>A question that has been often raised is: "Can one character do all the parts to the quest themselves?" No. You must be of the proper class in order to complete the class-specific quests leading up to this quest. Additionally, non Vah Shir can multiquest the citizenship quest and loop until they have enough faction to attempt various Shar Vahl quests, but for the class-specific quests, they may only complete the one for their own character class. (The other guilds will not allow them to complete their quests.)</i>
</p> 
<p>
<i>You'll also find several spots where details are sketchy. If you can help fill in the gaps, please <a href="http://mboards.eqtraders.com/phpBB2/viewforum.php?f=19">post details to the message boards</a>.</i>
</p> 
<p>
After each young Vah Shir completes their <a href="<!--server:x-->articles/article_page.php?article=q42&menustr=120070000000">citizenship quest</a>, their guild master starts them on a progressive set of tradeskill quests. Each class is directed toward a different tradeskill. Beastlords are assigned <a href="<!--server:x-->articles/article_page.php?article=q75&menustr=120070000000">tailoring tasks</a>, rogues are assigned <a href="<!--server:x-->articles/article_page.php?article=q76&menustr=120070000000">baking tasks</a>, shamen are given <a href="<!--server:x-->articles/article_page.php?article=q77&menustr=120070000000">brewing tasks</a>, warriors are set to <a href="<!--server:x-->articles/article_page.php?article=q78&menustr=120070000000">smithing</a>, and bards <a href="<!--server:x-->articles/article_page.php?article=q74&menustr=120070000000">create pottery</a>. 
</p> 
<p>
When each class completes all their assigned tasks, they are given a special no drop item (Rogues, Warriors and Bards recieved a no drop Hilt; Shaman recieve a no drop Shaft; Beastlords recieve a no drop claw) and sent to create their sonic wolf bane weapon (and, presumably, help those who help them to create their own weapons as well). This requires the assistance of Vah Shir from all other character classes, as each has to create an item that goes into the final weapon combine.
</p> 
<p>
The final combine of hilt/claw with the other needed parts is made in a purchased Weapons Assembly Kit (sold by Arms Historian Qua). There is no skill check on the final combine, but there are skill checks for each of the class-specific combines listed below.
</p> 
<p>
All the drop items are found in <a href="<!--server:x-->sources/source_zone_page.php?article=g89&menustr=110000000000&sz=1171">Hollowshade Moor</a>. Unless noted otherwise the owlbear items drop off owlbear cubs and grapplers (not owlbears in the caves) and the sonic wolf items drop off wandering sonic wolves (not off the sonic wolves in the caves).
</p> 
<p>
It appears that the combines for each of the items listed below is trivial in between 130 and 140 in the appropriate tradeskill. 
</p>
<ul>
<li>Beastlords must create <b>toughened sinew lashings</b>. Combine stretching dowel, owlbear tendons, sonic wolf tendons, kelp salts and fish oil soaked rags in any sewing kit to create toughened sinew lashings. Trivial for the combine is 135 tailoring. Owlbear tendons drop in Hollowshade Moor off the owlbear cubs and grapplers. Sonic wolf tendons appear to drop off any wandering sonic wolf in Hollowshade Moor. Kelp salts drop off the moor tortoises in Hollowshade Moor. Fish oil soaked rags are dropped off the grimling fisherman (and their chief), also in Hollowshade Moor. </li>
<li>Rogues must bake the <b>sonic wolf bane poison</b>. This requires: salass moss, tortoise saliva, sonic wolf blood, poison dart felt. Mix in these items in a no drop acrylia mortar & pestle. Combine the results with a posion vial and water in an oven<i>. </i>The digested salass moss is dropped off owlbear cubs and grapplers in Hollowshade Moor. The sonic wolf blood can drop off any wandering sonic wolf in Hollowshade Moor. The poison dart felts are dropped off the grimling spiritists in Hollowshade Moor. Toroise saliva is dropped off moor tortoises in, yep, you guessed it, Hollowshade Moor!</li>
<li>Shaman must brew a <b>reactive sealant soak</b>. This is done by combining blackened salt crystals, sonic wolf brain, crystalized ygri root, digested night palm, a water flask, and a <a href="<!--server:x-->items/show_item.php?item=5111">ceremonial strainer</a> (no drop) in a brew barrel. The blackened salt crystals are dropped off grimling mystics in Hollowshade Moor. Sonic wolf brain can be dropped by any wandering sonic wolf in Hollowshade Moor. Crystalized ygri root is a ground spawn near the sonic wolf caves in Hollowshade Moor. Digested night palm drops off the owlbear cubs in Hollowshade Moor.</li>
<li>Warriors must smith a <b>porous dagger or claw blade</b> (based upon which class is receiving the final weapon). This requires bag of white sand (no drop), powdered wolf claws (no drop), sonic wolf blood (no drop), chunk of porous ore, water flask, and either a blade mold or a claw mold, depending on which item you are making. The chunk of porous ore is a ground spawn in Hollowshade Moor, reported to be "just before the bridge" in Hollowshade Moor, "left over the hill". The white sand drops off grimling fishermen and grimling mystics in Hollowshade Moor. Powered wolf claws drop off wandering sonic wolves in Hollowshade, as does the sonic wolf blood. The molds are apparently given by an NPC, and further details are needed.</li>
<li>Bards mush create the <b>ceramic sleeves</b> using pottery. The ingredients are: ashes of dark ritual, flask of water, vial of owlbear bile, sonic wolf blood, black silt clay, sketch (NPC provided <a href="<!--server:x-->articles/article_page.php?article=q74&menustr=120070000000">see Bard Guide</a>) for claw or blade. Then fire with a quality firing sheet. The ashes of dark ritual drop off grimling spiritists in Hollowshade Moor. Owlbear bile is dropped off owlbear cubs and grapplers in Hollowshade. The sonic wolf blood can drop off any wandering sonic wolf in Hollowshade Moor. The black silt clay is a waters edge and possibly underwater ground spawn in Hollowshade Moor.</li>
</ul> 
<p>
When you have combined the appropriate claw/hilt and the 5 other items in the Weapons Assembly Kit, you must bring the resulting weapon and your Apprentice cloak (given during your class-specific questing), to the person who gave you the quest (this varies based on class). A more printable recipe, as well as the stats of the sonic wolf bane weapons <a href="../secrets/recipes_luclin.htm">can be found here.</a> You are then promoted to Journeyman status, given a new Journeyman's cloak and instructed to bring your cloak to Ahom Guzhin. Details on the continuation of this quest <a href="<!--server:x-->articles/article_page.php?article=q72&menustr=120040000000">can be found here</a>.
</p> 1115 2004-06-10 08:53:16 2003-06-10 11:31:40 G 0 0 2004-06-10 08:52:06 Ngreth Thergn

34 EQTC:Quests:MultiZone:PoTC Xanthe`s Earring of Nature/PoTC Quest <p>
This is an outline of the two versions of the quest for the Protection of the Cabbage spell (NO DROP, level 59, single-target Protection of the Grove spell for druids.) The original version of this quest, which relies very heavily on tradeskills, results in a copy of the spell and a no drop earring. The second version (also linked in below), results in only the spell. The earring reward is:
</p>
<blockquote> 
<p>
<!--item_op:1111..1..1..0-->
</p>
</blockquote>
<p>
If you have completed this quest and are not a druid, fear not! You can hand this earring back to Rebecca Cabbageleaf for:
</p>
<blockquote>
<p>
<!--item_op:1770..1..1..0-->
</p>
</blockquote>
<p>
<i>(Yes, druids can do this quest twice, first trading in their Xanthe's Earring of Nature for the Earring of the Solstice, <b>then</b> completing the quest a second time for the Xanthe's Earring of Nature. Remember to trade the Xanthe's earring in before attempting the second quest combine, due to the lore flag)</i>
</p>
<h3>Some basic background:</h3>
<p>
On May 8, 2002, during the massive tradeskill patch, nine Liber Brassica Felix books were introduced throughout the lands, each written in a different language. They outlined various "gifts" from the three druid races, and gave hints as to the proper combination of them. The folks here at EQTC and the druids from the Druid's Grove did <i>much</i> pooling of knowledge to solve this <i>extremely</i> tradeskill-intensive quest. It was the first cross-server quest of it's kind, and once it was completed, the folks at VI stated that there would become an easier path to obtaining the spell. They also stated that the quest would stay in place for those who wished to strive and obtain the extra reward. (The first person to complete the quest it was the lovely Lady Xanthe Ravenwolf on Bertoxxulous, which explains the new name for the earring.) At that time, the reward was the spell, and a lovely little ALL/ALL no drop earring.
</p>
<p>
On June 5, 2002 during another patch, the tenth Liber Brassica Felix book was found, and the old Earring of the Solstice magically changed into Xanthe's Earring of Nature in inventories throughout the lands. While greeted with some excitement, there was also much consternation by the non-druids in the community who suddenly found their all/all earring turn into something druid-only. Fortunately, VI took pity on all the frenzied tradeskillers who had spent the time and money to obtain the rather lovely earring, and announced partway through the day that Rebecca Cabbageleaf in Fungus Grove would be glad to accept trade-ins on earrings for something more suitable. (She could also be used to recharge earrings that were mistakenly out of charges, apparently by handing in the Xanthe's earring, then returning the Earring of the Solstice to her.)
</p>
<p>
<i><b>Please note that ALL of the "gifts" (and all the items that go into them) outlined in the links below are tradeable, so you can (and likely should) enlist the aid of grandmaster tradeskillers on your server for the items that are beyond your abilities.</b></i>
</p>
<h3>Version 1: the spell <i>and</i> earring</h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="<!--server:x-->articles/article_page.php?article=q127&menustr=120010000000">The Gifts of the Elves</a></li>
<li><a href="<!--server:x-->articles/article_page.php?article=q128&menustr=120010000000">The Gifts of Man</a></li>
<li><a href="<!--server:x-->articles/article_page.php?article=q129&menustr=120010000000">The Gifts of the Halflings</a></li>
<li><a href="<!--server:x-->articles/article_page.php?article=q124&menustr=120010000000">The Final Sacrifice</a></li>
<li><a href="<!--server:x-->articles/article_page.php?article=q123&menustr=120010000000">Liber Brassica Text</a> (the original clues from which the quest was solved)</li>
<li><a href="<!--server:x-->articles/article_page.php?article=q130&menustr=120010000000">PoTC Shopping List</a> (a master list of all ingredients needed to make all 9 gifts)</li>
</ul>

229 Weapon Charts from Geoux Geoux, from the Antonia Bayle server, has provided us with several xls files, for those who want an easily-printable chart of the crafted weapons in any given tier, including wield style, stats, etc. He, like us, has noted several inconsistencies and oddities in weapon progression and stats, as mentioned below.
<h4>Charts</h4>
<ul>
<li><a href="http://eq2.eqtraders.com/weaponsmith/tier2.xls">Tier 2 Crafted Weapons</a></li>
<li><a href="http://eq2.eqtraders.com/weaponsmith/tier3.xls">Tier 3 Crafted Weapons</a></li>
<li><a href="http://eq2.eqtraders.com/weaponsmith/tier4.xls">Tier 4 Crafted Weapons</a></li>
<li><a href="http://eq2.eqtraders.com/weaponsmith/tier5.xls">Tier 5 Crafted Weapons</a></li>
<li><a href="http://eq2.eqtraders.com/weaponsmith/tier6.xls">Tier 6 Crafted Weapons</a></li>
<li><a href="http://eq2.eqtraders.com/weaponsmith/tier7.xls">Tier 7 Crafted Weapons</a></li>
<li><a href="http://eq2.eqtraders.com/weaponsmith/tier8.xls">Tier 8 Crafted Weapons</a></li>
</ul>
<h4>Notes</h4>
<ul>
  <li> The Fulginate halberd (tier 5) is statistically wrong, compared to other 
    halberds. Expect this to be corrected in a future patch. </li>
  <li>The Adamantine trident (tier 7) also breaks pattern, but not as badly. It 
    should be 34 Str/Wis, not 17.</li>
  <li>The Adamantine scythe is statistically wrong, compared to other scythes. 
    Expect this to be corrected in a future patch.</li>
  <li>The Xegonite katar (tier 7) has no MP. It should have some; it?s what 
    the progression points to. Also, it?s description flags it as both a 
    1H slash and 1H crush. The Claw also flags as both slash and crush.</li>
  <li>The Xegonite ritual dagger has low HP on it. This doesn?t look intentional. 
    (60 instead of 16?)</li>
  <li>The Xegonite rapier?s secondary stats don?t make any sense compared 
    to other crafted rapiers.</li>
  <li>The Xegonite scimitar?s stats are wrong. It should have 42 H/MP, not 
    18 MP</li>
  <li>The Xegonite trident has stats for a xegonite 1H weapon. It should be twice what it is currently.</li>
  <li>The Ferrite battle hammer (tier 8) looks like it should have 55 H/MP, not 
    80 HP/30 MP. However, both ways it adds up to 110 H/MP combines. This may 
    be intentional.</li>
  <li>Both Tier 8 knuckles are leather-based instead of metal-based now. Is this 
    accident or intentional?</li>
  <li>Both Tier 8 katars are piercing instead of slashing now. Is this intended?</li>
  <li>The Ferrite ritual dagger has 80 HP/30 MP. This is probably reversed.</li>
  <li>The Ferrite leafblade and longsword probably have too many H/MP on them. 
    They have 70 HP/50 MP, should have 80 HP/30 MP or 55 H/MP.</li>
  <li>Both Tier 8 voulges are listed as 2H-piercing weapons. They are supposed 
    to be 1H pierce.</li>
  <li>The Ferrite tomahawk should be a str/sta/agi weapon, not a str/int weapon.</li>
  <li>Both Tier 8 scythes actually do more damage than the other 2H weapons. Intentional?</li>
  <li>The Incarnadine ritual dagger has 90 HP/45 MP. This should probably be reversed.</li>
  <li>Comparing the stat bonuses from the Ferrite weapons to the Incarnadine ones 
    makes me wonder if the Ferrite ones will be tuned down in the future. They?re 
    a huge jump from Adamantine, and not very far removed from Incarnadine. If 
    they do get ?nerfed?, it would probably be called for. As a weaponsmith, 
    of course I?d rather see the Incarnadine ones get boosted, but I don?t 
    think that would be very likely.</li>
  <li>In tier 7, they decided to make damage more interesting by varying the dmg/dly 
    ratios on their weapons, so it?s more than just combo 1 for 1-H weapons, 
    combo 2 for 2-H, and combo 3 for tridents. The ratings, however, remain the 
    same for all weapons in the category.</li>
  <li>Also in Tier 7, there appear to be no new weapons for that tier. All other 
    tiers, including tier 8, have new weapons each time. Having a gray background 
    in the Crafting Level box denotes them. It might be because of the fact they 
    got more creative with weapon damage, but there might be a couple new tier 
    7 plans down the road.</li>
  <li>There are a lot of unnecessary weapons that mirror each other now that dual 
    wield weapons have all been changed to one-handed. Examples of this are spears 
    and short spears. Expect a major weapon smith tradeskill patch in the future 
    to revise this. There?s also a good deal of weapon mirroring from when 
    your skills required specific weapon types to use (spears for Dragoon Spin, 
    for example). Now that all weapons will work with all skills, this could be 
    updated in the future.</li>
</ul>
<h4>Other notes from Geoux</h4>
<p>I?ve drawn all the information I used from the charts on EQ2411.com, look for future revisions of these tables on EQ2.EQTraders.com. These charts will print out on standard sized paper in landscape format. I hope this helps you, the weaponsmith, in choosing what you need to make!</p>
<p><a href="Sir_Razorback@comcast.net">Geoux, Berserker and Weaponsmith</a><br>
  Legacy of the Unsung<br>
  Antonia Bayle server<br>
   </p>
<p>If you have corrections, suggestions, or have better luck making it nice and readable on paper, by all means let me know! I know there?s some holes in Tier 8, hopefully I can get them patched soon!</p>

496 9thexpansion Chains of Eternity Announced This producer's letter was <a href="http://forums.station.sony.com/eq2/posts/list.m?topic_id=522020" target="_new">posted in the SOE forums</a> on September 6, 2012.
<blockquote>
  <p> Greetings Norrath! </p>
  <p>The time has come! We are very proud to announce our next expansion, EverQuest 
    II: Chains of Eternity! <br>
    The team is hard at work developing our ninth - yes, our ninth - expansion 
    and implementing the finer details, several of which I will go into here. 
    When the expansion launches, Norrathians will pass into Ethernere, the realm 
    of the afterlife, where all spirits pass after death on their way to their 
    final resting place.<br>
    <br>
    Recently, something has gone horribly wrong in Ethernere and it is bleeding 
    through in the mortal plane. Over the summer months, evidence of ripples between 
    the realms was in evidence as items with ethereal energy appeared upon the 
    dead. As the tears between the realms widen, it will be up to the heroes of 
    Norrath to save the immortal and mortal realms from collapse!<br>
    <br>
    The adventures in this expansion will be great ones! The team is spending 
    a lot of time ensuring that you experience the story, rather than merely read 
    it, so I won?t give it all away in this letter. As for features and 
    details, we?ve got a lot to crow about. We hope players enjoy it as 
    much as we?ve enjoyed weaving it together.<br>
    <br>
    Cross Over to More Content<br>
    In two re-imagined Ethernere overlands inspired by Feerrott and Loping Plains, 
    players will find a region in chaos. The natural ebb and flow of spirits passing 
    through the Ethernere to each spirit?s final resting place is corrupted 
    and on the edge of destruction, threatening every mortal?s life and 
    afterlife. Through the trials of nine new instanced dungeons, players will 
    attempt to mend the end of all things. Prelude content and dungeons give insights 
    into the threat from the other side while telling all new stories - including 
    advancing the story behind the Ages End Prophecy. Players meet new creatures 
    from the beyond and face a whole host of new challenges.<br>
    <br>
    Lots of Quests!<br>
    In this expansion, the signature, or main, storyline quest will be available 
    to everyone no matter how they play the game. Every player tough enough to 
    access the expansion content will have the opportunity to see how the story 
    ends, and raiding guilds will have opportunities to take part in special events 
    that support the story. Even when the main quest line completes, players gain 
    access to benefits as a result of their heroic acts and get rewards for replaying 
    content.<br>
    <br>
    Adventure and Tradeskill Levels Increased to 95<br>
    We are adding three more levels onto the cap which gives us a lot of opportunity 
    to create new spells, recipes, and Prestige Abilities, our next feature...<br>
    <br>
    Prestige Abilities<br>
    Each subclass will get access to new Prestige Abilities. Our engineering and 
    design teams are hard at work creating new abilities that will set a new bar 
    for players and for creating events. The new abilities give players more tools 
    to tinker with in combat, and designers too. <br>
    Tradeskill Prestige Abilities<br>
    We have started implementing Tradeskill Prestige abilities too. These allow 
    our tradeskill classes the ability to become specialists in their chosen craft 
    in a variety of ways. We?re still creating these and excited about the 
    opportunities that will open up for our tradeskillers!<br>
    <br>
    Guild Level to 95<br>
    To provide new benefits, we wanted to increase our Guild Levels . We will 
    speak more to that when we are further along with the implementation.<br>
    <br>
    Organic Adornments<br>
    We have a new adornment type in development! These Organic Adornments, as 
    the name suggests, will gain experience with the player and grow more powerful 
    as a result. There will be many to choose from so players can focus on how 
    they want to increase the power of their characters.<br>
    <br>
    Loot and more loot<br>
    Of course, there are going to be plenty of items in the expansion for players 
    to discover. This is a very strong content expansion with lots to do and find. 
    We heard our players ask for fewer features and more content that builds on 
    the core game so we?re doing just that.<br>
    <br>
    Extra content<br>
    At the same time as we?re focusing on the expansion, we are still offering 
    live content prior to the expansion. We are releasing the first areas of Sleeper?s 
    Tomb in mid-September which we refer to as the ?Prelude.? This 
    advances the world story as players find entry into the tomb. <br>
    <br>
    We have another event that we?re keeping under wraps that releases closer 
    to the expansion and then, of course, there?s ?Chains of Eternity? 
    itself releasing in November. We?re even releasing additional free content 
    at the same time that the expansion launches. Players will discover that avatars 
    are once again making an appearance in Norrath. These avatars are different 
    from those who appeared in the past.<br>
    <br>
    All in the all, the team is driving hard to bring the players awesome content 
    -- time and time again. I?m among a team of perfectionist gamers making 
    a game for gamers. It?s been incredible to see them work tirelessly 
    for excellence and everyone?s entertainment. Hard not to be romantic 
    about gaming...<br>
    <br>
    There?s more to come in the details, of course, but we have been bursting 
    at the seams to tell you what we can...and now we have.<br>
    <br>
    We invite you to come on this crazy ride with us. We really think you?ll 
    love it!</p>
</blockquote> 2012-09-06 11:23:05 2012-09-06 11:23:05 Niami Denmother 0 0
1 about EQ2TC Welcome to EQ2TC! <a href="http://www.wtfcomics.com" target="_new"><!--image:niami.jpg--></a><p>Welcome to EQ2 Traders Corner! For those of you who are just experiencing tradeskills for the first time, this is the proud "offspring" of EQTraders Corner (EQTC), the largest and oldest EQ tradesill sites in the world. Please remember to read the Visitors Corner message board threads before posting in the forums, as there are some rules of the road that guests are asked to follow, not only to keep things focused on tradeskills, but also to cut down on the massive workload involved in maintaining and updating this site.</p>

<h4>Who's Who?</h4>
<p><b>Niami DenMother ("Mum")</b> - founder/creator of EQTC, this wee redheaded halfling lady is prone to spurts of activity followed by long naps in various people's packs. (Don't forget to leave some chocolate in there for her!).  Due to fibromyalgia and rheumatoid arthritis, those naps are a pretty vital part of the creative process!</p>

<p><b>Ngreth Thergn("The House Ogre" or "the hubbyogre")</b> - Mum's RL husband and reason why EQ2TC was born. He did much of the physical web design for the sites, and while his current job doesn't allow him to do much commentary on the forums, he continues to be the person that keeps Mum balanced ...or at least as balanced as a redhead ever is!</p>
<p><b>FTC guidelines require that we disclose to you that Niami DenMother's RL husband is an employee of Daybreak Games.  Nonetheless, the opinions and other posts expressed here are those of the EQtraders staff and not of anyone at Daybreak Games.</b></p>
<h4>Why Did We Do It?</h4>
<p>Originally, given the high cost in time and money of running EQTC, Mum said a flat-out "NO!" when asked about an EQ2 site. However, the House Ogre can be quite convincing when he wishes, so we decided we'd give it a try and hope for the best.  Things have changed a lot since then - on his job front, on Mum's energy front, on how crafting works in the game, etc., but somehow, we keep plugging along. </p>

<p>Bear with me, and please pardon any out-of-date-articles. I do writing spurts in chunks as time and energy allow. In the meantime, browse the How To section of the site, wander the forums, and join me for an exploration of the addiction that is crafting in EQII!</p>
<p>There are times when crafting makes us all a bit crazy, and I'm no exception. <b><a href="http://www.eqtraders.com/articles/article_page.php?article=g277">Here's an old, old (2004) page</a></b> of just how crazy it can be!</p>

108 adorn Adornments and You The adornment system that was released with the Echoes of Faydwer expansion is quite a bit for many folks to wrap their brains around at first glance (or even third or fourth glance), so 'Mum has been busy digging out some extra mental wrapping paper! Hopefully we can take this in small enough steps that you'll end up with a nice pretty package when we are done with this mini-lesson, not just some messy snarl of tape, brain, ribbons, and wrapping paper.
<p>Perhaps the best way to start, is to <b><font color=<blue">think of the adornment system as a way of creating semi-permanent buffs for gear.</font></b> In the end, that is basically what it will boil down to, anyway - items that crafters make that can then be placed on specific types and levels of gear.</p>
<p><b><font color=<blue">Every single tradeskill class will have something that they can make with the adornment system</font></b>. Not every class will have even close to the same number/type of adornments, but everyone can make something, eventually.</p>
<p><b><font color=<blue">Adornments are tradeable, and can be applied by anyone</font></b>. All adornments can be traded, and any player can apply them to the appropriate gear.</p>
<p><b><font color=<blue">Every adornment is meant for a specific slot and minimum level of gear.</font></b> Each adornment is used only in one specific gear slot, and can only be placed on a certain minimum level of the gear (NOT the level of the player, but the gear). So, a level 30 ear adornment, could be applied to an earring that was level 30 or higher, but not to a level 29 earring.</p>
<p><b><font color=<blue">Every adornment recipe requires special resources that are created by the transmute process.</font></b> When gear is broken down with transmuting, tier-specific special resources are created that are only used to craft adornments. The resources are tradeable, so you don't have to be a transmuter to make adornments. It is beyond helpful to have a transmuter as part of your crafting alt-army, to break down ingredients for yourself, but contrary to a widely-held misconception, you do not have to be a transmuter to make adornments.</p>
<h3>Adornments and the Crafter</h3>
When able, we will get out a master list of which class makes which adornments. However, the system was receiving tweaks right up until launch, and our lists are hopelessly tangled and incorrect. We're working on it as we get the proper recipe drops distributed to the classes that can use them.
<p>In the meantime, however, let me give you a few examples to help you get this settled in your mind. An alchemist might make some "polish" that can be applied to rings that increases your resistance to something, such as a fiery polish that has a +vs heat boost on it. A jeweler, on the other hand, might make a "clasp" for a neck slot item that increases the effects of all heal spells, while a provisioner makes a "fastening" for a wrist item that grants +STR.  And so on.</p>
<h4>Ingredients and Naming</h4>
If, using the above example of a fiery polish, we were to make the item, it would have a different prefix name, and use different ingredients, based on the tier of the recipe. A flickering fiery polish would be the tier 1 version, for example, while the tier 7 version would be a scintillating fiery polish. The tier 1 version of it would be likely to use ulteran powder and lapis fragments, while the tier 7 version would use illusionary powder and lunar fragments.
<table width="95%" border="1" cellpadding="2">
  <tr> 
    <td><strong>tier</strong></td>
    <td><strong>adorn prefix</strong></td>
    <td><strong>Powder</strong></td>
    <td><strong>Fragment</strong></td>
    <td><strong>Infusion</strong></td>
    <td><strong>Mana</strong></td>
  </tr>
  <tr> 
    <td>1</td>
    <td>flickering</td>
    <td>ulteran</td>
    <td>lapis</td>

    <td>refined</td>
  </tr>

    <td>shimmering</td>
    <td>aether</td>
    <td>coral</td>
    <td>air</td>
    <td>processed</td>
  </tr>
  <tr> 
    <td>3</td>
    <td>sparkling</td>
    <td>phantom</td>
    <td>jasper</td>
    <td>fire</td>
    <td>clarified</td>
  </tr>
  <tr> 
    <td>4</td>
    <td>glimmering</td>
    <td>ethereal</td>
    <td>opal</td>
    <td>water</td>
    <td>purified</td>
  </tr>
  <tr> 
    <td>5</td>
    <td>luminous</td>
    <td>spectral</td>
    <td>ruby</td>
    <td>nightmares</td>
    <td>natural</td>
  </tr>
  <tr> 
    <td>6</td>
    <td>lambent</td>
    <td>vision</td>
    <td>pearl</td>
    <td>daydreams</td>
    <td>coalesced</td>
  </tr>
  <tr> 
    <td>7</td>
    <td>scintillating</td>
    <td>illusionary</td>
    <td>lunar</td>
    <td>illusion</td>
    <td>hardened</td>
  </tr>
</table>
Let us just step back from that for a moment. It will make much more sense once we have some confirmed recipes to look at.  Instead, let us take a quick look at this from the customer end.
<h3>Adornments and the End-User</h3>
Everyone and their cousin's cousin will be wanting adornments. Please realize that the supplies won't always be easy to come by, recipes won't always be easy to come by, and your crafter is likely to be as confused, or even more confused than you are, with regards to what can/cannot be made by whom.
<p>Every crafting profession gets <b>different</b> adornment recipes from every other crafting profession, and it is not always easy to tell at a glance which crafter you will need in order to adorn a specific item with what you want. What you want may not even be an option.</p>
<p>Take several deep breaths, let the crafters catch up, and start edumacating yourself now on some of the easier details to sort out. Adornments are tradeable and do NOT require any crafting skill to apply.  To apply the adornment, you right-click on it and select the use option, then mouse over the item that you wish to adorn. If the cursor is outlined in red, that item cannot be adorned for one of <i>several reasons</i>. If it is outlined in blue, you are clear to use the adornment on the item.
<ol><li>Items must be fully repaired before you try to adorn them</li>
<li>Items must be of equal or <b>higher</b> level than the adornment you are trying to put on it. It if says level 30 on the adornment, it can only be placed on an appropriate item that is level 30 or higher.</li>
<li>Adornments are permanent. Once you place the adornment on an item, there is no getting it back. 
<li>Any stat changing effects from an adornment will display on the item in blue text. Any proc will be listed in the proper spell effects section on the item.</li>
<li>One adornment per item. Placing a second adornment on an item deletes the original adornment and replaces it with the new one.</li>
<li>Every adornment is targeted at a specific gear slot - no trying to put an adornment for an ear slot on your bracelet.</li>
<li>Not all gear can be adorned, even if you match up the level and slot correctly. Imbued gear cannot be adorned until after GU32 goes live. Certain quest rewards, such as items in the Claymore quest line, cannot be adorned, etc.  Any item that displays as "ORNATE" cannot be imbued.</li>
</ol>
There will be more written on this subject, however, please realize that the folks that are trying to get this all set out in a coherent format are still trying to wrap <i>their</i> brains around it enough to explain it to others. Please DO post questions/comments to our forums with specific confusions, error corrections, and so on...
<h3>Take Note - Quality Matters!</h3>
One important thing to note is that quality matters ... kind of.  Every adornment recipe will show you a secondary result (byproduct) when you examine it. As well as the adornment itself, you will recieve back one or more of the ingredients used in the recipe, based on the quality level completed. While the amount returned for tier 1 adornments isn't that impressive, every little bit helps, and it really adds up when you're finishing off a tier 7 adornment and getting back a half dozen (wild guess, I don't remember numbers) of the fragments that went into the creation of the item.
<h3>Class-Specific Adornment Guides?</h3>
One of our community members, Lucutious of Najena, with the help of the community, put together adornment charts for his guild's wiki, with information sorted by tradeskill class and by slot.  Rather than try to duplicate his efforts, he's been kind enough to give us a link to the master adornment guide. Check out this wonderful <a href="http://www.deadzed.com/pe/wiki/index.php?title=Category:Adornment" target="_New">Master Adornment Guide</a>.  You can also find a more compacted master chart, without a lot of the extra bells and whistles on the <a href="http://www.britlore.co.uk/eq2/adornments.php" target="_new">Britannic Lore site</a>. 44 alchemrecipe Recipes - Alchemy The fumes of the chemistry table are all in a day's work for Alchemists, a level 20+ sub-class of Scholar that specializes in potions, poisons, and essences (fighter skill upgrades).<hr> 2006-06-10 11:31:33 2004-12-07 05:18:39 Niami Denmother 0 1 2009-01-26 11:39:01 Niami Denmother
82 ALH Curt Schilling and SoE Help Raise Money for ALS Association <h3>CURT SCHILLING ENTERS A WORLD OF FANTASY DURING RED SOX-YANKEES SERIES JUNE 5, 6, 7</h3>
<h4>World Series MVP Debuts in the Virtual World of EverQuest II As an Evil Villain and Helps to Raise Money for ALS Association</h4>
<!--image:schillingnpc.jpg-->
SAN DIEGO, CA ' May 24, 2006 ' Sony Online Entertainment LLC (SOE), a global leader in the online video games industry, today announced that Boston Red Sox pitcher Curt Schilling is about to debut in his favorite online video game, EverQuest II, as an epically awesome, loot-dropping virtual bad guy who battles unwary players.  And it's all for a good cause.
<p>Schilling's video game character will reside within the online world of EverQuest II (EQII) for three days during the Yankees vs. Red Sox baseball series June 5, 6 and 7, 2006 at Yankee Stadium.  During this time, anyone can register for and log into EverQuest II at www.battleals.com to challenge the evil Schilling character, appropriately named 'Curt Schilling.'  
</p><p>
Every time a player defeats the virtual Schilling character, Sony Online Entertainment, creators of EverQuest II, will make a donation of $5 dollars (up to a maximum of $10,000) to the ALS Association, which assists patients with ALS, also known as Lou Gehrig's Disease.  After the three-day baseball series, Curt's character will remain within the game as a high-powered enemy that characters will have to face later in the game.  At the launch of the campaign on June 5th, Schilling's 10-year-old son, Gehrig (named after the legendary Yankee first baseman), will be one of the first to battle his virtual dad in-game.
</p><p>
In addition, SOE will encourage its hundreds of thousands of EQII players to type /ALS within the game in order to donate money to Curt's charity of choice, the ALS Association.  This program will run for the entire three-day series and will give the SOE player community a chance to help with this worthy cause.
</p><p>
"ALS is about as devastating a disease as you can imagine," says Schilling. "It's relentless, ruthless, and devastates entire families as one member slowly perishes.  With video games exploding in popularity, I can't think of a better place to reach the masses to raise awareness.'
</p><p>
ALS is no stranger to baseball; it's more commonly known as Lou Gehrig disease, named after the New York Yankees infielder whose Hall of Fame career was cut short by the degenerative nerve disease.  Lou Gehrig played in 2,130 consecutive games before ALS stopped him, a feat matched only by Baltimore Orioles shortstop Cal Ripken Jr.  Curt Schilling and wife Shonda have been involved in the fight against ALS for more than a decade.  Shonda serves on the board of directors of ALS Association's (ALSA) Greater Philadelphia and Arizona Chapters and advocates for ALS patients with members of Congress.
</p><p> 
Schilling may be one of today's top athletes in professional baseball, but off the field he spends time playing with his son in the award-winning Massively Multiplayer Online (MMO) video game EverQuest II -- a fully realized 3D fantasy world of mythical creatures, magic spells, majestic landscapes, and fierce dragons -- since the game's creation.
</p><p>
EverQuest II offers players a huge online world where thousands of players come together for shared adventure and community.  This online game sets the standard for graphical realism, as players are immersed in the game's exciting locales and dangerous lands. EverQuest II has a powerful epic storyline and gives players the potential to be hero or villain in a world that never ends. 
</p><p>
'I enjoy the anonymity and the ability to interact on a personal level with people I wouldn't normally meet or know,' Schilling said. 'That, and the game is a riot. There's no end to it, the world is enormous, the possibilities are endless, and above all else, it's a place to go and relax amongst friends. What I can't get enough of is your ability to interact with real live people. The game's about teamwork, and knowing the right way to pick and play your class properly in such a way that it complements a group. That's why EverQuest has stayed so popular.'
</p><p>
The 39-year-old baseball superstar has been a long time fan of SOE games, even contributing game reviews of expansion packs to gaming magazines, and is an avid web communicator, feeling this is the best way to connect with the video game fans.
</p> 2006-05-24 07:10:08 2006-05-24 07:01:45 Niami Denmother 0 0 2006-05-24 07:08:31 Niami Denmother
104 altars Furniture - Altars The Echoes of Faydwer expansion introduced several new quest series regarding the return of the gods. These quests allow players to help the gods regain power in the lands, make sacrifices at that deity's altar in return for favor that can be used to call down miracles and the like, and so on. 
<p>While a deity revamp is still in the works, another good-only gooddess, Erollisi Marr, was added in 2015 to the list of those who could be worshipped.</p>
<p>On top of the altars being quest rewards within the deity progression, there are carpenter-made versions of the altars.  The common (tier 4) altars look the same as the basic altar rewarded in each deity quest line, and the rare (tier 7) "imbued" altars looks the same as the advanced altars that are given out later in each quest series. (The crafted altars reduce your purchase cost for blessings and miracles in comparison to the quested altars - see chart below the images for details.)</p>
<p>All crafted altars are no value. There is no status rent reduction tied to these house items. In addition, <b>altars cannot be placed in guild halls</b>, due to how the worship system is handled.  However, there is a "shrine" version of these altars that is purely decorative, for use in guild halls and homes alike. These decorative shrines</p>
<p>No trade recipe books for the altars are sold on special Deity Historian NPCs at the BBM docks and in front of the Kelethin Library.</p>
<p>Common altars (level 35 recipes) use: <b>9 severed briarwood, 2 feyiron clusters, 1 etched leather pelt, 8 garnet sandpaper</b>.  The rare ("imbued") altars (level 65 recipes) use: <b>1 rough lumbered ebony, 14 rough lumbered rosewood, 3 adamantine clusters, 2 horned leather pelts, 20 acrylia sandpaper</b>.</p>

<p>In each of the below images, the common altar is on the left, the rare version is on the right.</p>

<p></p>
<h3>So, I Have an Altar - Now What?</h3>
Deities reward their faithful worshippers with various blessings and miracles, each of which has a specific favor cost assigned to it. This favor is earned by performing specific quests for your deity, as well as sacrificing various items of value at an altar dedicated to that deity.  Crafted altars reduce the favor cost of such blessings and miracles, in comparison to their quested counterparts.
<p>
This list also include the Blessed altar, a dropped altar that has the same graphic as the crafted rare imbued altar, and the Ordained altar. (The Ordained altar is a fabled no-trade drop from Mayong Mistmoore - thanks, Faush, for the added details!).</p>
Numbers used in the below are comparing the first available blessing and miracle. Blessings and miracles vary in cost based on which one you select, but the percentage discount should stay the same for any specific altar type.

<h3>Shrines</h3>
As mentioned above, the way worship at altars is handled made it so that altars are not allowed to be placed in guild halls.  An additional carpenter-only recipe book (Decorative Deity Shrines) was added to the Deity Historian NPCs containing recipes for purely decorative shrines that can be placed in the guildhall.  Decorative means that they cannot be used for worship, but you can place them for looks.  In addition, each of these shrines have extra particle effects that you do not see with the common or imbued version, making them even more impressive decorations than their more humble counterparts.
<p>The recipes are level 65, and require 3 rough lumbered rosewood, 2 adamantine cluster, 1 horned leather pelt and 10 acrylia sandpaper.  The finished shrines have 100 rent status reduction when placed in a home.</p>
